   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Legatum Prosperity Index</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <p>The <b>Legatum Prosperity Index</b> is an annual ranking developed by the Legatum Institute, a division of the private investment firm <a href="/wiki/Legatum" title="Legatum">Legatum</a>. The ranking is based on a variety of factors including wealth, <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a>, education, health, <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">personal well-being</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a>. </p>
      <p>As of the 2019 rankings, 166 countries and territories were ranked, and <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> topped the list overall and for <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific" title="Asia-Pacific">Asia-Pacific</a> (9th overall) and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> for <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> (12th overall). <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a> was in last place. In 2013, twenty-seven of the top 30 countries were democracies.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Methodology">Methodology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legatum_Prosperity_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Methodology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The 2018 Legatum Prosperity Index is based on 104 different variables analysed across 149 nations around the world. Source data includes <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup World Poll</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Development_Indicators" title="World Development Indicators">World Development Indicators</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">International Telecommunication Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fragile_States_Index" title="Fragile States Index">Fragile States Index</a>, <a href="/wiki/Worldwide_Governance_Indicators" title="Worldwide Governance Indicators">Worldwide Governance Indicators</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom house">Freedom House</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Values_Survey" title="World Values Survey">World Values Survey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_international" class="mw-redirect" title="Amnesty international">Amnesty International</a>, Centre for Systemic Peace. The 104 variables are grouped into 9 sub-indexes, which are averaged using equal weights. The 9 sub-indexes are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Economic Quality</li> 
       <li>Business Environment</li> 
       <li>Governance</li> 
       <li>Education</li> 
       <li>Health</li> 
       <li>Safety &amp; Security</li> 
       <li>Personal Freedom</li> 
       <li>Social Capital</li> 
       <li>Natural Environment</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>For example, Personal Freedom includes freedom of speech and religion, national tolerance for immigrants and ethnic and racial minorities. The Social Capital sub-index includes the percentage of citizens who volunteer, give to charity, help strangers, and who feel they can rely on family and friends. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Oxford_Analytica" title="Oxford Analytica">Oxford Analytica</a> assisted in the early development of the Prosperity Index and has contributed to shaping the methodology. Today, the annual Index is produced and published by the Legatum Institute. </p>
      <p>The Legatum Institute operates a transparent approach to its work on the Prosperity Index. To that end, the entire methodology of the Prosperity Index along with the data used to create it is available for free online at the institute's website. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings_and_scores_by_country">Rankings and scores by country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legatum_Prosperity_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Rankings and scores by country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legatum_Institute">Legatum Institute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legatum_Prosperity_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Legatum Institute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Legatum_Institute" title="Legatum Institute">Legatum Institute</a> publishes the index. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">Personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legatum_Prosperity_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Director of the Prosperity Index is Dr. Stephen Brien. The Prosperity Index is reviewed and critiqued by an advisory panel of academics and scholars representing a range of disciplines and includes: <a href="/wiki/Tim_Besley" title="Tim Besley">Prof Tim Besley</a> (<a href="/wiki/London_school_of_economics" class="mw-redirect" title="London school of economics">London School of Economics</a>); <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Drezner" class="mw-redirect" title="Daniel Drezner">Dr. Daniel Drezner</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tufts_University" title="Tufts University">Tufts University</a>); <a href="/wiki/Carol_Graham" title="Carol Graham">Dr. Carol Graham</a> (<a href="/wiki/Brookings_Institution" title="Brookings Institution">Brookings Institution</a>); Dr. Edmund Malesky (<a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Diego" title="University of California, San Diego">University of California, San Diego</a>); Dr. Ann Owen (<a href="/wiki/Hamilton_College_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamilton College (New York)">Hamilton College</a>). </p>
      <p>The Legatum Institute's International Advisory Group also contributes and assists in the Prosperity Index: Prof Peter Skerry (<a href="/wiki/Boston_college" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston college">Boston College</a>); Prof Dan Chirot (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington" title="University of Washington">University of Washington</a>); Toby Mundy CEO (<a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Books" title="Atlantic Books">Atlantic Books</a>); and Patrick Cheung. </p>
